      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">
        Demography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Demography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Population">
        Population
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Population">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_in_the_Americas_by_population" title="List of countries in the Americas by population">
        List of countries in the Americas by population
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The total population of the Americas is about 951 million people and is divided as follows:
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2010)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        North America: 565 million (includes Central America and the
        <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">
         Caribbean
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        South America: 386 million
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_urban_centers">
        Largest urban centers
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Largest urban centers">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Largest_cities_in_the_Americas" title="Largest cities in the Americas">
        Largest cities in the Americas
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_the_Americas_by_population" title="List of metropolitan areas in the Americas by population">
        List of metropolitan areas in the Americas by population
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       There are three urban centers that each hold titles for being the largest population area based on the three main demographic concepts:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wider_103-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-wider-103">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/City_proper" title="City proper">
         City proper
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        A city proper is the locality with legally fixed boundaries and an administratively recognized urban status that is usually characterized by some form of local government.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
         <a href="#cite_note-104">
          [102]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
         <a href="#cite_note-105">
          [103]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
         <a href="#cite_note-106">
          [104]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
         <a href="#cite_note-107">
          [105]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
         <a href="#cite_note-108">
          [106]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">
         Urban area
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        An urban area is characterized by higher population density and vast human features in comparison to areas surrounding it. Urban areas may be cities, towns or conurbations, but the term is not commonly extended to rural settlements such as villages and hamlets. Urban areas are created and further developed by the process of urbanization and do not include large swaths of rural land, as do metropolitan areas.
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">
         Metropolitan area
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        Unlike an urban area, a metropolitan area includes not only the urban area, but also satellite cities
        <i>
         plus intervening rural land
        </i>
        that is socio-economically connected to the urban core city, typically by employment ties through commuting, with the urban core city being the primary labor market.
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       In accordance with these definitions, the three largest population centers in the Americas are:
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">
        Mexico City
       </a>
       , anchor to the largest metropolitan area in the Americas; New York City, anchor to the largest urban area in the Americas; and São Paulo, the largest city proper in the Americas. All three cities maintain
       <a href="/wiki/Global_city#Alpha" title="Global city">
        Alpha
       </a>
       classification and large scale influence.
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">
        Mexico City
       </a>
       is the largest city in the Americas and the
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">
        Western Hemisphere
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">
        Northern Hemisphere
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional center">
       <li class="gallerycaption">
        Urban centers within the Americas
       </li>

        <div style="width: 265px">

           </a>

          </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnology">
        Ethnology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Ethnology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">

      <p>
       The population of the Americas is made up of the descendants of four large
       <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">
        ethnic groups
       </a>
       and their combinations.
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">
         Indigenous peoples of the Americas
        </a>
        , being
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amerindian" title="Amerindian">
         Amerindians
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">
         Inuit
        </a>
        , and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aleut_people" title="Aleut people">
         Aleuts
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Those of European ancestry, mainly Spanish, British and Irish,
        <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">
         Portuguese
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">
         German
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">
         Italian
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">
         French
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_people" title="Polish people">
         Polish
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_(ethnic_group)" title="Dutch (ethnic group)">
         Dutch
        </a>
        , Russians and
        <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">
         Scandinavians
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Those of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-American_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Afro-American peoples of the Americas">
         African
        </a>
        ancestry, mainly of West African descent.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">
         Asians
        </a>
        , that is, those of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Asia" title="Eastern Asia">
         Eastern
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">
         South
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">
         Southeast Asian
        </a>
        ancestry.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">
         Mestizos
        </a>
        (
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metis_people" title="Metis people">
         Metis people
        </a>
        in Canada), those of mixed European and Amerindian ancestry.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Mulatto" title="Mulatto">
         Mulattoes
        </a>
        , people of mixed African and European ancestry.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Zambo" title="Zambo">
         Zambos
        </a>
        (Spanish) or
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cafuso" title="Cafuso">
         Cafusos
        </a>
        (Portuguese), those of mixed African and Amerindian ancestry.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       The majority of the population live in
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">
        Latin America
       </a>
       , named for its predominant cultures, rooted in
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Romance-speaking_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Romance-speaking Europe (page does not exist)">
        Latin Europe
       </a>
       (including the two dominant languages, Spanish and
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       , both
       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">
        Romance languages
       </a>
       ), more specifically in the
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">
        Iberian
       </a>
       nations of
       <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">
        Portugal
       </a>
       and Spain (hence the use of the term
       <a href="/wiki/Ibero-America" title="Ibero-America">
        Ibero-America
       </a>
       as a synonym). Latin America is typically contrasted with
       <a href="/wiki/Anglo-America" title="Anglo-America">
        Anglo-America
       </a>
       , where English, a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Germanic_language" title="Germanic language">
        Germanic language
       </a>
       , is prevalent, and which comprises Canada (with the exception of
       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_French" title="Canadian French">
        francophone Canada
       </a>
       rooted in Latin Europe [France]—see
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Québec">
        Québec
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Acadia" title="Acadia">
        Acadia
       </a>
       ) and the United States. Both countries are located in North America, with cultures deriving predominantly from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon" title="Anglo-Saxon">
        Anglo-Saxon
       </a>
       and other
       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">
        Germanic
       </a>
       roots.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
        Religion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Religion">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Latin_America" title="Religion in Latin America">
        Religion in Latin America
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_North_America" title="Religion in North America">
        Religion in North America
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christianity_in_the_Americas" title="Christianity in the Americas">
        Christianity in the Americas
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_the_Americas" title="Islam in the Americas">
        Islam in the Americas
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The most prevalent faiths in the Americas are as follows:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Christianity (86 percent)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
         <a href="#cite_note-119">
          [117]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <ul>
         <li>
          Roman Catholicism: Practiced by 69 percent
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pewlat_120-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-pewlat-120">
            [118]
           </a>
          </sup>
          of the Latin American population, 81 percent
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pewlat_120-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-pewlat-120">
            [118]
           </a>
          </sup>
          in Mexico and 61 percent
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pewlat_120-2">
           <a href="#cite_note-pewlat-120">
            [118]
           </a>
          </sup>
          in Brazil whose Roman Catholic population of 123 million is the greatest of any nation's; approximately 24 percent of the United States' population
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIAWFB_121-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-CIAWFB-121">
            [119]
           </a>
          </sup>
          and about 39 percent of Canada's.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-religion2011d_122-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-religion2011d-122">
            [120]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </li>
         <li>
          Protestantism: Practiced mostly in the United States, where half of the population are Protestant, Canada, with slightly more than a quarter of the population, and Greenland; there is a growing contingent of
          <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">
           Evangelical
          </a>
          and
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentecostal" title="Pentecostal">
           Pentecostal
          </a>
          movements in predominantly Catholic Latin America.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
           <a href="#cite_note-123">
            [121]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">
           Eastern Orthodoxy
          </a>
          : Found mostly in the United States (1 percent) and Canada; this Christian group is growing faster than many other Christian groups in Canada and now represents roughly 3 percent of the Canadian population.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-religion2011d_122-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-religion2011d-122">
            [120]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-denominational_Christianity" title="Non-denominational Christianity">
           Non-denominational Christians
          </a>
          and other Christians (some 1,000 different Christian denominations and sects practiced in the Americas).
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">
         Irreligion
        </a>
        : About 12 percent, including atheists and agnostics, as well as those who profess some form of spirituality but do not identify themselves as members of any organized religion)
       </li>
       <li>
        Islam: Together, Muslims constitute about 1 percent of the North American population and 0.3 percent of all Latin Americans. It is practiced by 3 percent
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-religion2011d_122-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-religion2011d-122">
          [120]
         </a>
        </sup>
        of Canadians and 0.6 percent of the U.S. population.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIAWFB_121-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-CIAWFB-121">
          [119]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">
         Argentina
        </a>
        has the largest Muslim population in Latin America with up to 600,000 persons, or 1.9 percent of the population.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stateirf_124-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-stateirf-124">
          [122]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Judaism (practiced by 2 percent of North Americans—approximately 2.5 percent of the U.S. population and 1.2 percent of Canadians
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
         <a href="#cite_note-125">
          [123]
         </a>
        </sup>
        —and 0.23 percent of Latin Americans—Argentina has the largest Jewish population in Latin America with 200,000 members)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
         <a href="#cite_note-126">
          [124]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Other faiths include
       <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">
        Buddhism
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">
        Hinduism
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">
        Sikhism
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bahá'í Faith">
        Bahá'í Faith
       </a>
       ; a wide variety of indigenous religions, many of which can be categorized as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animist" title="Animist">
        animistic
       </a>
       ;
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_age" title="New age">
        new age
       </a>
       religions and many
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_traditional_religion" title="African traditional religion">
        African
       </a>
       and African-derived religions.
       <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">
        Syncretic
       </a>
       faiths can also be found throughout the Americas.
      </p>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">
        Languages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Languages">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">
        Indigenous languages of the Americas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_North_America" title="Languages of North America">
        Languages of North America
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_South_America" title="Languages of South America">
        Languages of South America
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="691" data-file-width="624" height="244" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png/220px-Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png/330px-Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png/440px-Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Languages spoken in the Americas
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Various
       <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">
        languages
       </a>
       are spoken in the Americas. Some are of European origin, others are spoken by indigenous peoples or are the mixture of various idioms like the different creoles.
      </p>
      <p>
       The most widely spoken language in the Americas is
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
        <a href="#cite_note-137">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The dominant language of
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">
        Latin America
       </a>
       is Spanish, though the most populous nation in Latin America,
       <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">
        Brazil
       </a>
       , speaks
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       . Small enclaves of
       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
        French
       </a>
       -,
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">
        Dutch
       </a>
       - and
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       -speaking regions also exist in Latin America, notably in
       <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">
        French Guiana
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">
        Suriname
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">
        Belize
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">
        Guyana
       </a>
       respectively.
       <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole" title="Haitian Creole">
        Haitian Creole
       </a>
       is dominant in the nation of
       <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">
        Haiti
       </a>
       , where French is also spoken.
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">
        Native languages
       </a>
       are more prominent in Latin America than in
       <a href="/wiki/Anglo-America" title="Anglo-America">
        Anglo-America
       </a>
       , with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nahuatl_language" title="Nahuatl language">
        Nahuatl
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quechua_languages" title="Quechua languages">
        Quechua
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Aymara_language" title="Aymara language">
        Aymara
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_language" title="Guaraní language">
        Guaraní
       </a>
       as the most common. Various other native languages are spoken with less frequency across both Anglo-America and Latin America.
       <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">
        Creole languages
       </a>
       other than Haitian Creole are also spoken in parts of Latin America.
      </p>
      <p>
       The dominant language of Anglo-America is English. French is also official in
       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
        Canada
       </a>
       , where it is the predominant language in
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">
        Quebec
       </a>
       and an official language in
       <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">
        New Brunswick
       </a>
       along with English. It is also an important language in
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">
        Louisiana
       </a>
       , and in parts of
       <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">
        New Hampshire
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">
        Maine
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">
        Vermont
       </a>
       . Spanish has kept an ongoing presence in the
       <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_United_States" title="Southwestern United States">
        Southwestern United States
       </a>
       , which formed part of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Spain" title="Viceroyalty of New Spain">
        Viceroyalty of New Spain
       </a>
       , especially in
       <a href="/wiki/Californio" title="Californio">
        California
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">
        New Mexico
       </a>
       , where
       <a href="/wiki/New_Mexican_Spanish" title="New Mexican Spanish">
        a distinct variety of Spanish
       </a>
       spoken since the 17th century has survived. It has more recently become widely spoken in other parts of the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       because of heavy immigration from Latin America. High levels of immigration in general have brought great linguistic diversity to Anglo-America, with over 300 languages known to be spoken in the United States alone, but most languages are spoken only in small enclaves and by relatively small immigrant groups.
      </p>
      <p>
       The nations of Guyana, Suriname, and Belize are generally considered
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">
          <span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (July 2012)">
           by whom?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       not to fall into either Anglo-America or Latin America because of their language differences from Latin America, geographic differences from Anglo-America, and cultural and historical differences from both regions; English is the primary language of Guyana and Belize, and Dutch is the primary language of Suriname.
      </p>
      <p>
       Most of the non-native languages have, to different degrees, evolved differently from the mother country, but are usually still mutually intelligible. Some have combined, however, which has even resulted in completely new languages, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Papiamento" title="Papiamento">
        Papiamento
       </a>
       , which is a combination of Portuguese, Spanish, Dutch (representing the respective colonizers), native
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arawak_peoples" title="Arawak peoples">
        Arawak
       </a>
       , various
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_languages" title="African languages">
        African languages
       </a>
       , and, more recently English. The
       <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">
        lingua franca
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Portu%C3%B1ol" title="Portuñol">
        Portuñol
       </a>
       , a mixture of Portuguese and Spanish, is spoken in the border regions of Brazil and neighboring Spanish-speaking countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
        <a href="#cite_note-138">
         [136]
        </a>
       </sup>
       More specifically,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riverense_Portu%C3%B1ol_language" title="Riverense Portuñol language">
        Riverense Portuñol
       </a>
       is spoken by around 100,000 people in the border regions of Brazil and
       <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">
        Uruguay
       </a>
       . Because of
       <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">
        immigration
       </a>
       , there are many communities where other languages are spoken from all parts of the world, especially in the United States, Brazil,
       <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">
        Argentina
       </a>
       , Canada,
       <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">
        Chile
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">
        Costa Rica
       </a>
       and Uruguay—very important destinations for immigrants.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
        <a href="#cite_note-139">
         [137]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
        <a href="#cite_note-140">
         [138]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
        <a href="#cite_note-141">
         [139]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">

       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>

         </a>
        </td>
        <td style="background:#f7f7f7;">
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0000FF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>

         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">

         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">

        <td style="background:#ffffff;">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LocationNSAm3.png">
          <img alt="LocationNSAm3.png" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="800" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/LocationNSAm3.png/100px-LocationNSAm3.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/LocationNSAm3.png/150px-LocationNSAm3.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/LocationNSAm3.png/200px-LocationNSAm3.png 2x" width="100"/>
         </a>
        </td>
        <td style="background:#f7f7f7;">
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0000FF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          North America (NA)
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #8080FF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          May be included in NA
         </div>
         <p>
          <span style="white-space:nowrap; font-size:90%;">
           <span style="background:#0000FF;">
            <span class="nowrap">
            </span>
           </span>
           <span style="background:#8080FF;">
            <span class="nowrap">
            </span>
           </span>
           Northern America
          </span>
         </p>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00FFFF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Middle America (MA)
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #8DE1E1; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Caribbean (may be
          <br/>
          <span class="nowrap">
          </span>
          <span style="position:relative; bottom:0.4em;">
           included in MA)
          </span>
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FEB900; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          South America (SA)
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00FF00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          May be included
          <br/>
          <span class="nowrap">
          </span>
          <span style="position:relative; bottom:0.4em;">
           in MA or SA
          </span>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="background:#ffffff;">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LocationNSAngloLatin.png">
          <img alt="LocationNSAngloLatin.png" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="800" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/LocationNSAngloLatin.png/100px-LocationNSAngloLatin.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/LocationNSAngloLatin.png/150px-LocationNSAngloLatin.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/LocationNSAngloLatin.png/200px-LocationNSAngloLatin.png 2x" width="100"/>
         </a>
        </td>
        <td style="background:#f7f7f7;">
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #2D5F2C; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Anglo-America (A-A)
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00C080; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          May be included in A-A
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFD800; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Latin America (LA)
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFFC00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          May be included in LA
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Americas_(terminology)" title="Americas (terminology)">
        Americas (terminology)
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="English">
        English
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: English">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/American_(word)" title="American (word)">
        American (word)
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        Speakers of English
       </a>
       generally refer to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landmass" title="Landmass">
        landmasses
       </a>
       of North America and South America as
       <i>
        the Americas
       </i>
       , the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">
         Western Hemisphere
        </a>
       </i>
       , or the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">
         New World
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
        <a href="#cite_note-142">
         [140]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The adjective
       <i>
        American
       </i>
       may be used to indicate something pertains to the Americas,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OEDAMERICAN_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-OEDAMERICAN-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but this term is primarily used in English to indicate something pertaining to the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OEDAMERICAN_3-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-OEDAMERICAN-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
        <a href="#cite_note-143">
         [141]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxfcdn_144-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-oxfcdn-144">
         [142]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some non-ambiguous alternatives exist, such as the adjective
       <i>
        Pan-American
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
        <a href="#cite_note-145">
         [143]
        </a>
       </sup>
       or
       <i>
        New Worlder
       </i>
       as a demonym for a resident of the closely related
       <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">
        New World
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OED|New_Worlder_4-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-OED|New_Worlder-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Use of
       <i>
        America
       </i>
       in the hemispherical sense is sometimes retained, or can occur when translated from other languages.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
        <a href="#cite_note-146">
         [144]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For example, the
       <a href="/wiki/Association_of_National_Olympic_Committees" title="Association of National Olympic Committees">
        Association of National Olympic Committees
       </a>
       (ANOC) in Paris maintains a single continental association for "America", represented by one of the five
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympic_rings" title="Olympic rings">
        Olympic rings
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
        <a href="#cite_note-147">
         [145]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       American linguist
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/H.L._Mencken" title="H.L. Mencken">
        H.L. Mencken
       </a>
       said, " The Latin-Americans use Norteamericano in formal writing, but, save in Panama, prefer nicknames in colloquial speech."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mencken_148-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mencken-148">
         [146]
        </a>
       </sup>
       To avoid "American" one can use constructed terms in their languages derived from "United States" or even "North America".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxfcdn_144-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-oxfcdn-144">
         [142]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">
        <a href="#cite_note-149">
         [147]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">
        <a href="#cite_note-150">
         [148]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In Canada, its southern neighbor is often referred to as "the United States", "the U.S.A.", or (informally) "the States", while U.S. citizens are generally referred to as "Americans".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxfcdn_144-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-oxfcdn-144">
         [142]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most Canadians resent being referred to as "Americans".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxfcdn_144-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-oxfcdn-144">
         [142]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish">
        Spanish
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Spanish">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In Spanish,
       <i>
        América
       </i>
       is a single continent composed of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subcontinent" title="Subcontinent">
        subcontinents
       </a>
       of
       <i>
        América del Sur
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        América del Norte
       </i>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Land_bridge" title="Land bridge">
        land bridge
       </a>
       of
       <i>
        América Central
       </i>
       , and the islands of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Antilles" title="Antilles">
         Antillas
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <i>
        Americano
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        americana
       </i>
       in Spanish refers to a person from
       <i>
        América
       </i>
       in a similar way that
       <i>
        europeo
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        europea
       </i>
       refers to a person from
       <i>
        Europa
       </i>
       . The terms
       <i>
        sudamericano/a
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        centroamericano/a
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        antillano/a
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        norteamericano/a
       </i>
       can be used to more specifically refer to the location where a person may live.
      </p>
      <p>
       Citizens of the United States of America are normally referred to by the term
       <i>
        estadounidense
       </i>
       (rough literal translation: "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Statesian" title="United Statesian">
        United Statesian
       </a>
       ") instead of
       <i>
        americano
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        americana
       </i>
       which is discouraged,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-norteamerica_151-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-norteamerica-151">
         [149]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estadosunidos_152-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-estadosunidos-152">
         [150]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the country's name itself is officially translated as
       <i>
        Estados Unidos de América
       </i>
       (United States of America), commonly abbreviated as
       <i>
        Estados Unidos
       </i>
       (EEUU).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estadosunidos_152-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-estadosunidos-152">
         [150]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Also, the term
       <i>
        norteamericano
       </i>
       (North American) may refer to a citizen of the United States. This term is primarily used to refer to citizens of the United States, and less commonly to those of other North American countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-norteamerica_151-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-norteamerica-151">
         [149]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese">
        Portuguese
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Portuguese">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In Portuguese,
       <i>
        <a class="extiw" href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Am%C3%A9rica" title="pt:América">
         América
        </a>
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AmericaPortBE_153-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AmericaPortBE-153">
         [151]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is a single continent composed of
       <i>
        América do Sul
       </i>
       (South America),
       <i>
        América Central
       </i>
       (Central America) and
       <i>
        América do Norte
       </i>
       (North America).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AmericaME_154-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AmericaME-154">
         [152]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It can be ambiguous, as
       <i>
        América
       </i>
       can be used to refer to the United States of America, but is avoided in print and formal environments.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EstadosUnidosIt_155-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-EstadosUnidosIt-155">
         [153]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EstadosUnidosESPN_156-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-EstadosUnidosESPN-156">
         [154]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="French">
        French
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: French">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In French the word
       <i>
        américain
       </i>
       may be used for things relating to the Americas; however, similar to English, it is most often used for things relating to the United States.
       <i>
        Panaméricain
       </i>
       may be used as an adjective to refer to the Americas without ambiguity.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">
        <a href="#cite_note-157">
         [155]
        </a>
       </sup>
       French speakers may use the noun
       <i>
        Amérique
       </i>
       to refer to the whole landmass as one continent, or two continents,
       <i>
        Amérique du Nord
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Amérique du Sud
       </i>
       . In French,
       <i>
        Amérique
       </i>
       is also used to refer to the United States, making the term ambiguous. Similar to English usage,
       <i>
        les Amériques
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        des Amériques
       </i>
       is used to refer unambiguously to the Americas.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dutch">
        Dutch
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Dutch">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In Dutch, the word
       <i>
        Amerika
       </i>
       mostly refers to the United States.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Although the United States is equally often referred to as
       <i>
        de Verenigde Staten
       </i>
       ("the United States") or
       <i>
        de VS
       </i>
       ("the US"),
       <i>
        Amerika
       </i>
       relatively rarely refers to the Americas, but it is the only commonly used Dutch word for the Americas. This often leads to ambiguity; and to stress that something concerns the Americas as a whole, Dutch uses a combination, namely
       <i>
        Noord- en Zuid-Amerika
       </i>
       (North and South America).
      </p>
      <p>
       Latin America is generally referred to as
       <i>
        Latijns Amerika
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Midden-Amerika
       </i>
       for Central America.
      </p>
      <p>
       The adjective
       <i>
        Amerikaans
       </i>
       is most often used for things or people relating to the United States. There are no alternative words to distinguish between things relating to the United States or to the Americas. Dutch uses the local alternative for things relating to elsewhere in the Americas, such as
       <i>
        Argentijns
       </i>
       for
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Argentine_people" title="Argentine people">
        Argentine
       </a>
       , etc.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Multinational_organizations">
        Multinational organizations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Multinational organizations">

        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The following is a list of multinational organizations in the Americas.
      </p>

      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <p>
       The U.S. has the fastest-growing economy in the Americas according to a 2016 study conducted by the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">
        International Monetary Fund
       </a>
       (IMF),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFUNASURGDP_159-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-IMFUNASURGDP-159">
         [157]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFNorthAmericaGDP_160-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-IMFNorthAmericaGDP-160">
         [158]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and has the highest GDP per capita in the Americas as well.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFNorthAmericaGDP_160-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-IMFNorthAmericaGDP-160">
         [158]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFUNASURGDP_159-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-IMFUNASURGDP-159">
         [157]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Countries in the northern part of the Americas tend to have healthier and stronger economies than countries in the southern part of the Americas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFNorthAmericaGDP_160-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-IMFNorthAmericaGDP-160">
         [158]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFUNASURGDP_159-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-IMFUNASURGDP-159">
         [157]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2016, five to seven countries in the southern part of the Americas had weakening economies in decline, compared to only three countries in the northern part of the Americas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFNorthAmericaGDP_160-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-IMFNorthAmericaGDP-160">
         [158]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFUNASURGDP_159-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-IMFUNASURGDP-159">
         [157]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Haiti has the lowest GDP per capita in the Americas, although its economy was growing slightly as of 2016.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFNorthAmericaGDP_160-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-IMFNorthAmericaGDP-160">
         [158]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFUNASURGDP_159-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-IMFUNASURGDP-159">
         [157]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

          ). McArthur, Tom, ed., 1992. New York: Oxford University Press, p. 33: "[16c: from the feminine of
          <i>
           Americus
          </i>
          , the Latinized first name of the explorer Amerigo Vespucci (1454–1512). The name
          <i>
           America
          </i>
          first appeared on a map in 1507 by the German cartographer Martin Waldseemüller, referring to the area now called Brazil]. Since the 16c, a name of the western hemisphere, often in the plural
          <i>
           Americas
          </i>
          and more or less synonymous with
          <i>
           the New World
          </i>
          . Since the 18c, a name of the United States of America. The second sense is now primary in English: ... However, the term is open to uncertainties: ..."

           </i>

           <q>
            The part of the Earth comprising North and South America and surrounding waters; longitudes 20°W and 160°E are often considered its boundaries
           </q>

          </a>

          </a>

          <a href="/wiki/Valpara%C3%ADso" title="Valparaíso">

          </a>
